Top, the age distribution of each superfamily of subclass I of the Class II transposons (the terminal inverted repeat transposons). Bottom, the age distribution of LTR-RT superfamilies.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig4"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature22380/figures/4" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature22380/MediaObjects/41586_2017_Article_BFnature22380_Fig4_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 2 The density of LTR-RTs in 1 Mb bins per chromosome.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p>The scale represents a fraction, where 1.0 is 100% of a given bin.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig5"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature22380/figures/5" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature22380/MediaObjects/41586_2017_Article_BFnature22380_Fig5_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 3 Comparison of grape–sunflower–artichoke–coffee–lettuce genomes.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p>Top, dot plots of orthologues between the grape genome (<i>y</i> axis, as a representative of the <i>n</i> = 21 post-γ ancestor) and, from left to right, the sunflower (1–6 chromosomal relationships inherited from WGT-1 and WGD-2), artichoke (1–3 chromosomal relationships deriving from WGT-1), coffee (1–1 chromosomal relationships illustrating the absence of a coffee-specific WGD, despite WGT-1) genomes and the lettuce genetic map (1–3 chromosomal relationships deriving from WGT-1). Bottom, dot plots of orthologues between the sunflower genome (<i>y</i> axis, <i>n</i> = 17 chromosomes) and artichoke (<i>x</i> axis, <i>n</i> = 17 chromosomes) and lettuce (<i>x</i> axis, <i>n</i> = 9 chromosomes) genomes with 1–1 chromosomal relationships.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig6"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature22380/figures/6" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature22380/MediaObjects/41586_2017_Article_BFnature22380_Fig6_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 4 Organ-specific expression in the sunflower transcriptome.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, Histogram of the specificity index Tau in expressed genes. <b>b</b>, Box plot distribution of the specificity index Tau in 11 different organs. The different organs are represented with the following colours: Ray floret ovary, dark brown; disc floret corolla, orange; ray floret ligule, yellow; bract, bright green; stem, dark green; pistil, bright blue; roots, dark blue; leaves, light green; disc floret ovary (seeds), red; stamens, magenta; pollen, light blue. <b>c</b>, Violin plot of the specificity index Tau for transcription factors (TFs, magenta) and long non-coding RNA (lncRNA, light blue). <b>d</b>, Cumulative bar plot showing the organ distribution of specific genes (left), transcription factors (middle) and lncRNA (right). Colours are the same as in <b>b</b>.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig7"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature22380/figures/7" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature22380/MediaObjects/41586_2017_Article_BFnature22380_Fig7_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 5 Integrative analysis of flowering time.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, Flowering time network in the sunflower. Flowering time genes of <i>A. thaliana</i> and their interactions are drawn in green. Sunflower genes and orthology relationships with <i>A. thaliana</i> genes are shown in orange. <b>b</b>, Genomic architecture of flowering time in the domesticated sunflower. Outer ring, location of genomic regions associated with flowering time. Inner ring, links between ohnologues of a sunflower-specific whole-genome duplication (WGD-2), limited to genes located in regions associated with flowering time. Links between ohnologues of WGD-2 that are both located in regions associated with flowering time are drawn in red, other links are drawn in grey. <b>c</b>, Pathway of the integration of flowering signals in meristem (simplified pathway adapted from ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Bouché, F., Lobet, G., Tocquin, P. &amp; Périlleux, C. FLOR-ID: an interactive database of flowering-time gene networks in Arabidopsis thaliana. Nucleic Acids Res. 44 (D1), D1167–D1171 (2016)" href="/articles/nature22380#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d38746e2750">20</a>). The bright orange backgrounds indicate genes for which at least one sunflower orthologue was located in a region associated with flowering time. Bold italic genes indicates genes for which we identified additional in-paralogues compared to a previous study using more limited genomic data<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Blackman, B. K. et al. Contributions of flowering time genes to sunflower domestication and improvement. Genetics 187, 271–287 (2011)" href="/articles/nature22380#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d38746e2755">21</a></sup>. Simple arrows represent positive regulation and other arrows negative regulation. Curved lines between genes represent protein–protein complexes.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="supp-item" id="Fig8"><h3 class="c-article-supplementary__title u-h3"><a class="print-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view supplementary info" data-track-label="link" data-test="supp-info-link" href="/articles/nature22380/figures/8" data-supp-info-image="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fnature22380/MediaObjects/41586_2017_Article_BFnature22380_Fig8_ESM.jpg">Extended Data Figure 6 Integrative analysis of oil metabolism.</a></h3><div class="c-article-supplementary__description" data-component="thumbnail-container"><p><b>a</b>, Whole-metabolic network (3,821 reactions and 475 pathways). Genes are coloured by expression levels in developing seeds. <b>b</b>, Co-expression network of oil metabolic pathway. Genes that co-localize with QTLs are coloured in orange. <b>c</b>, Sub-network with genes from <b>b</b> co-localizing with QTLs. Node size is proportional to <i>F</i><sub>st</sub> between lines cultivated for oil production and other domesticated lines. Genes with an <i>F</i><sub>st</sub> in the top 5% are coloured in dark orange. <b>d</b>, Mapping of candidate genes (orange genes from <b>c</b>) on the pathways of diacylglycerol and triacylglycerol biosynthesis. <b>e</b>, Mapping of candidate genes on the pathway of linoleate biosynthesis. <b>f</b>, Tree of a gene cluster including a candidate gene of the PAP2 superfamily, involved in the synthesis of fatty acid precursors (<b>d</b>). Athal, <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i>; Brapa, <i>Brassica rapa</i>; Ccard, <i>Cynara cardunculus</i>; Hvulg, <i>Hordeum vulgare</i>; Osati, <i>Oryza sativa</i>; Ptrich, <i>Populus trichocarpa</i>.</p></div></div><div class="c-article-supplementary__item" data-test="supp-item"><div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1"><figure><figcaption class="c-article-table__figcaption"><b id="Tab1" data-test="table-caption">Extended Data Table 1 Link between the genomic architecture of flowering time and the most recent whole-genome duplication experienced by the sunflower</b></figcaption><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="table-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="view table" data-track-label="button" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/nature22380/tables/1"><span>Full size table</span><svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-chevron-right"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec18" data-title="Supplementary information"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec18-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec18">Supplementary information</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec18-content"><div data-test="supplementary-info">

            <aside><div class="c-article-editorial-summary__container" data-component-show-more="true" id="editorial-summary"><section><h1 class="c-article-editorial-summary__title u-h3">Editorial Summary</h1><h2 class="c-article-editorial-summary__article-title">Sunflower genome</h2><div class="c-article-editorial-summary__content c-article-editorial-summary__content--less"><p>Nicolas Langlade and colleagues report the genome sequence of the domesticated sunflower, <i>Helianthus annuus</i> L., a global oil crop that can maintain stable yields across a wide range of environmental conditions. Their comparative analyses provide insights into the evolutionary history of Asterids. They also analysed transcriptomic data from vegetative and floral organs, re-sequenced 80 domesticated lines and performed genome-wide association studies identifying 35 loci associated with flowering time. These resources will be useful in breeding programs as well as ecological and evolutionary studies.</p></div></section></div></aside>
